                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بَدَا</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بد</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بدا</orth>
                  </form>, (T, S, M, &amp;c.,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَبْدُو</foreign>, (S, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بُدُوٌّ</foreign> (S, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَدْوٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءٌ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءَةٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَدًا</foreign>, (M, on the authority of Sb,) for which last we find, in [some of] the copies of the K, <foreign lang="ar">بُدُوٌّ</foreign>, a repetition, (TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">بُدُوْءٌ</foreign>, (so in other copies of the K,) <hi rend="ital">It appeared; it became apparent, open, manifest, plain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evident:</hi> (T, S, M, Msb, K:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n2037-1" target="تبدّى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n2041"/></foreign> [signifies the same; or <hi rend="ital">he showed himself,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it showed itself;</hi> (see an ex. in art. <foreign lang="ar">جيش</foreign>, voce <foreign lang="ar">جَاشَ</foreign>, last sentence;) or] <hi rend="ital">he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, came in sight,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">within sight.</hi> (KL.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَهُ فِى الأَمْرِ</foreign>, (T, M, Msb, K, and Har p. 665,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَدْوٌ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَدًا</foreign> (M, and so in a copy of the K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءٌ</foreign>, (T, M, and so in the CK,) or <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَدَاةٌ</foreign>; (as in some copies of the K;) or   
      <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَهُ فِى الأَمْرِ <ref cref="n2037-2" target="بَدَآءٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n1959"/></foreign>, (S, IB,) the last word being in the nom. case because it is the agent; (IB, TA;) <hi rend="ital">An opinion presented itself,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">occurred, to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">arose in his mind,</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">نَشَأَ</foreign>, (S, K, and Har ubi suprà,) or <hi rend="ital">appeared to him,</hi> (M,) [<hi rend="ital">respecting the affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">different from his first opinion, so that it turned him therefrom:</hi> (Har ubi suprà:) or <hi rend="ital">there appeared to him, respecting the affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case, what did not appear at first:</hi> (Msb:) accord. to Fr,   
      <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لِى <ref cref="n2037-3" target="بَدَآءٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n1959"/></foreign> means <hi rend="ital">another opinion appeared to me:</hi> accord. to Az, <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لِى بَدًا</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">my opinion changed from what it was.</hi> (TA.) Esh-Shemmàkh says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَعَلَّكَ وَ المَوْعُودُ حَقٌّ وَفَاؤُهُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَكَ فِى تِلْكَ القَلُوصِ بَدَآءُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">May-be</hi> (<hi rend="ital">but it is right that the promise be fulfilled</hi>) <hi rend="ital">an opinion different from thy first opinion hath arisen in thy mind respecting that youthful she-camel</hi>]. (M, TA.) <foreign lang="ar">ثُمَّ بَدَا لَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا رَأَوُا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱلْآيَاتِ لَيَسْجُنَنَّهُ</foreign>, in the Kur [xii.35], means <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَهُمْ <ref cref="n2037-4" target="بَدَآءٌ" n="4" type="6" subtype="FTFSO" lang="ar" select="n1959"/> وَقَالُوا لَيَسْجُنُنَّهُ</foreign>, [i.e. <hi rend="ital">Then an opinion arose in their minds, after they had seen the signs</hi> of his innocence, <hi rend="ital">and they said that they should certainly imprison him,</hi>] because <foreign lang="ar">ليسجننّه</foreign>, being a proposition, cannot be the agent: so says Sb. (M.) <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لِلّهِ أَنْ يَقْتُلَهُمْ</foreign>, occurring in a trad., means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">God determined that He would slay them:</hi> for, as IAth says, <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءٌ</foreign> signifies the <hi rend="ital">deeming to be right a thing that is known after its having been not known;</hi> and this may not be attributed to God: but as is said by Suh, in the R, one may say, [of God,] <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ يَفْعَلَ كَذَا</foreign>, [properly signifying <hi rend="ital">It occurred to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">appeared to him, that he should do such a thing,</hi>] as meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He desired to do such a thing;</hi> [as also <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا لَهُ فِى فِعْلِ كَذَا</foreign>;] and thus the phrase in the trad., here mentioned, has been explained. (TA.) [One says also, <foreign lang="ar">اِفْعَلْ كَذَا مَا بَدَا لَكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Do thou thus as long as it seems fit to thee:</hi> see, a verse of El-Ahmar cited voce <foreign lang="ar">جَلَّ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا القَوْمُ</foreign>, (T, S, M, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَدْوٌ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">بَدَآءٌ</foreign>; (M, K;) [the latter of which is said in the TA to be the right;] or <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا إِلَى البَادِيَةِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَدَاوَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِدَاوَةٌ</foreign>; (Msb;) <hi rend="ital">The people, or company of men, went forth to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَادِيَة</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">or desert</hi>]: (M, Msb, K:) or, the former, <hi rend="ital">went forth to their</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَادِيَة</foreign>: (S:) or <hi rend="ital">went forth from the region, or district, of towns or villages or of cultivated land, to the pasturingplaces in the deserts:</hi> (T:) [ISd says,] <foreign lang="ar">بَدْوٌ</foreign> may be used as meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِدَاوَةٌ</foreign>, which is the <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حِضَارَةٌ</foreign>: (M:) [J says,] <foreign lang="ar">بَدَاوَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِدَاوَةٌ</foreign> signify the <hi rend="ital">dwelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abiding, in the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَادِيَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">desert</hi>]; the <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حِضَارَةٌ</foreign>: but Th says, I know not <foreign lang="ar">بَدَاوَةٌ</foreign>, with fet-h, except on the authority of AZ alone: (S:) As says that <foreign lang="ar">بداوة</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حضارة</foreign> are with kesr to the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> and fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ح</foreign>; but AZ says the reverse, i. e. with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> and kesr to the <foreign lang="ar">ح</foreign>: (T:) both are also explained as signifying the <hi rend="ital">going forth to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَادِيَة</foreign>: and some mention <foreign lang="ar">بُدَاوَةٌ</foreign>, with damm; but this is not known: (TA:)   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n2037-5" target="تبدّى" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n2041"/></foreign> like wise signifies <hi rend="ital">he went forth from the constant sources of water to the places where herbage was to be sought</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in the desert</hi>]; (T;) or <hi rend="ital">he dwelt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode, in the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَادِيَة</foreign>. (S, K.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ بَدَا جَفَا</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">He who abides in the desert becomes rude, rough, coarse,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uncivil, like the desert-Arabs.</hi> (S.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ يَبْدُو إِلَى هٰذِهِ التِّلَاعِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He used to go forth to these water-courses in the desert,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">these high grounds, </hi> or <hi rend="ital">low grounds,</hi> &amp;c.]. (TA.)         <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">بَدَا</foreign>
